
<a name="6.00"></a>
<p><h3>6.00 Introduction to Computer Science and Programming
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/rest.gif" alt="Rest Elec in Sci & Tech" title="Rest Elec in Sci & Tech" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 3-7-2
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.00"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW3-4.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-100</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>TBA</i> <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to computer science and programming for students with little or no programming experience.  Students learn how to program and how to use computational techniques to solve problems.  Topics include software design, algorithms, data analysis, and simulation techniques.  Assignments are done using the Python programming language. Meets with 6.0001 first half of term and 6.0002 second half of term. Credit cannot also be received for 6.0001 or 6.0002. Final given during final exam week.
<br><I>J. V. Guttag</I><br><a href="javascript:PopUpHelp('http://eduapps.mit.edu/textbook/books.html?Term=2018FA&Subject=6.00');" >Textbooks (Fall 2017)</a></font>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.0001"></a>
<p><h3>6.0001 Introduction to Computer Science Programming in Python
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">); first half of term
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 2-3-1
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.0001"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> Ends Oct 20. <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW3-4.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-100</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to computer science and programming for students with little or no programming experience. Students develop skills to program and use computational techniques to solve problems. Topics include the notion of computation, Python, simple algorithms and data structures, testing and debugging, and algorithmic complexity. Combination of 6.0001 and 6.0002 counts as REST subject. Final given in the seventh week of the term.
<br><I>J. V. Guttag</I><br><a href="javascript:PopUpHelp('http://eduapps.mit.edu/textbook/books.html?Term=2018FA&Subject=6.0001');" >Textbooks (Fall 2017)</a></font>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.0002"></a>
<p><h3>6.0002 Introduction to Computational Thinking and Data Science
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">); second half of term
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.0001">6.0001</a> or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 2-3-1
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.0002"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> Begins Oct 23. <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW3-4.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-100</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Provides an introduction to using computation to understand real-world phenomena. Topics include plotting, stochastic programs, probability and statistics, random walks, Monte Carlo simulations, modeling data, optimization problems, and clustering. Combination of 6.0001 and 6.0002 counts as REST subject. Final given during final exam week.
<br><I>J. V. Guttag</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.002"></a>
<p><h3>6.002 Circuits and Electronics
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/rest.gif" alt="Rest Elec in Sci & Tech" title="Rest Elec in Sci & Tech" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p2" title="8.02, 8.021, 8.022">8.02</a>; <I><a href="m18a.html#18.03">18.03</a> or <a href="m2a.html#2.087">2.087</a></I>
<br>Units: 4-1-7
<br>Credit cannot also be received for <A HREF="m6a.html#6.S064">6.S064</A>
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.002"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-101</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>TBA</i> <b>Recitation:</b> <i>WF11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-310</a>) or <i>WF12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-310</a>) or <i>WF1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-310</a>) or <i>WF2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-310</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Fundamentals of the lumped circuit abstraction. Resistive elements and networks, independent and dependent sources, switches and MOS devices, digital abstraction, amplifiers, and energy storage elements. Dynamics of first- and second-order networks; design in the time and frequency domains; analog and digital circuits and applications. Design exercises. Occasional laboratory.
<br><I>A. Agarwal, J. del Alamo, J. H. Lang, D. J. Perreault</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->

<a name="6.003"></a>
<p><h3>6.003 Signals and Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/rest.gif" alt="Rest Elec in Sci & Tech" title="Rest Elec in Sci & Tech" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p2" title="8.02, 8.021, 8.022">8.02</a>; <a href="m2a.html#2.087">2.087</a> or <a href="m18a.html#18.03">18.03</a>
<br>Units: 5-0-7
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.003"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-101</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>TBA</i> <b>Recitation:</b> <i>WF10</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-210</a>) or <i>WF11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-210</a>) or <i>WF1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=36">36-144</a>) or <i>WF2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=36">36-144</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Presents the fundamentals of signal and system analysis. Topics include discrete-time and continuous-time signals, Fourier series and transforms, Laplace and Z transforms, and analysis of linear, time-invariant systems. Applications drawn broadly from engineering and physics, including audio and image processing, communications, and automatic control.
<br><I>D. M. Freeman, Q. Hu, J. S. Lim</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.004"></a>
<p><h3>6.004 Computation Structures
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/rest.gif" alt="Rest Elec in Sci & Tech" title="Rest Elec in Sci & Tech" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br>URL: <a href="http://6004.mit.edu/">http://6004.mit.edu/</a>
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.004"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=10">10-250</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>WF10</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-301</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=13">13-4101</a>) or <i>WF11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-301</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=13">13-4101</a>) or <i>WF12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-303</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=36">36-155</a>) or <i>WF1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-303</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=36">36-155</a>) or <i>WF2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-303</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=13">13-5101</a>) or <i>WF3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-303</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=13">13-5101</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces architecture of digital systems, emphasizing structural principles common to a wide range of technologies. Multilevel implementation strategies; definition of new primitives (e.g., gates, instructions, procedures, and processes) and their mechanization using lower-level elements. Analysis of potential concurrency; precedence constraints and performance measures; pipelined and multidimensional systems. Instruction set design issues; architectural support for contemporary software structures.
<br><I>C. J. Terman, D. Sanchez, S. Z. Hanono Wachman</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.006"></a>
<p><h3>6.006 Introduction to Algorithms
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.042">6.042</a>; <a href="m6a.html#6.0001">6.0001</a> or <I><a href="m6a.html#6.009">6.009</a></I>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.006"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-100</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>WF10</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-304</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-302</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=35">35-310</a>) or <i>WF11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-304</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-302</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=36">36-155</a>) or <i>WF12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-301</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-304</a>) or <i>WF1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-304</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=5">5-134</a>) or <i>WF2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=5">5-134</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=35">35-310</a>) or <i>WF3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=35">35-310</a>) or <i>WF4</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=35">35-310</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to mathematical modeling of computational problems, as well as common algorithms, algorithmic paradigms, and data structures used to solve these problems. Emphasizes the relationship between algorithms and programming, and introduces basic performance measures and analysis techniques for these problems.
<br><I>R. L. Rivest, S. Devadas</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.007"></a>
<p><h3>6.007 Electromagnetic Energy: From Motors to Solar Cells
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">) <img src="/icns/rest.gif" alt="Rest Elec in Sci & Tech" title="Rest Elec in Sci & Tech" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p2" title="8.02, 8.021, 8.022">8.02</a>; <I><a href="m2a.html#2.087">2.087</a> or <a href="m18a.html#18.03">18.03</a></I>
<br>Units: 5-1-6
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.007"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MWF1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-141</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>T EVE (7-9 PM)</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=38">38-601</a>) or <i>W EVE (7-9 PM)</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=38">38-601</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Discusses applications of electromagnetic and equivalent quantum mechanical principles to classical and modern devices. Covers energy conversion and power flow in both macroscopic and quantum-scale electrical and electromechanical systems, including electric motors and generators, electric circuit elements, quantum tunneling structures and instruments. Studies photons as waves and particles and their interaction with matter in optoelectronic devices, including solar cells and displays.
<br><I>V. Bulovic, R. J. Ram</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.008"></a>
<p><h3>6.008 Introduction to Inference
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=m2" title="18.02, 18.02A, 18.022, 18.023, 18.024">18.02</a> or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 4-4-4
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.008"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW10</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-155</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>TBA</i> <b>Recitation:</b> <i>TR10</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-303</a>) or <i>TR1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-302</a>) or <i>TR2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-302</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces probabilistic modeling for problems of inference and machine learning from data, emphasizing analytical and computational aspects. Distributions, marginalization, conditioning, and structure; graphical representations. Belief propagation, decision-making, classification, estimation, and prediction. Sampling methods and analysis. Introduces asymptotic analysis and information measures. Computational laboratory component explores the concepts introduced in class in the context contemporary applications. Students design inference algorithms, investigate their behavior on real data, and discuss experimental results.
<br><I>P. Golland, G. W. Wornell</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.009"></a>
<p><h3>6.009 Fundamentals of Programming
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.0001">6.0001</a>
<br>Units: 2-4-6
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.009"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>T9.30-11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=54">54-100</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>F10-12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=1">1-190</a>) or <i>F1-3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=6">6-120</a>) or <i>F9-11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-141</a>) or <i>F1-3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-155</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>W9-11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=56">56-154</a>) or <i>W1-3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-370</a>) or <i>W9-11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=2">2-190</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces fundamental concepts of programming. Designed to develop skills in applying basic methods from programming languages to abstract problems. Topics include programming and Python basics, computational concepts, software engineering, algorithmic techniques, data types, and recursion and tail recursion. Lab component consists of software design, construction, and implementation of design.
<br><I>A. Chlipala, S. Devadas, C. J. Terman</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.01"></a>
<p><h3>6.01 Introduction to EECS via Robotics
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.0001">6.0001</a> or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 2-4-6
<br>URL: <a href="http://mit.edu/6.01/index.html">http://mit.edu/6.01/index.html</a>
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.01"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>T9.30-11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-270</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>T11-12.30,R2-5</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-501</a>) or <i>T2-3.30,R9.30-12.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-501</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>An integrated introduction to electrical engineering and computer science, taught using substantial laboratory experiments with mobile robots. Key issues in the design of engineered artifacts operating in the natural world: measuring and modeling system behaviors; assessing errors in sensors and effectors; specifying tasks; designing solutions based on analytical and computational models; planning, executing, and evaluating experimental tests of performance; refining models and designs. Issues addressed in the context of computer programs, control systems, probabilistic inference problems, circuits and transducers, which all play important roles in achieving robust operation of a large variety of engineered systems.
<br><I>D. M. Freeman, A. Hartz, L. P. Kaelbling, T. Lozano-Perez</I><br>No textbook information available
<a name="6.011"></a>
<p><h3>6.011 Signals, Systems and Inference
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.003">6.003</a>; <a href="m6a.html#6.008">6.008</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.041A">6.041A</a>, or <a href="m18b.html#18.600">18.600</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Covers signals, systems and inference in communication, control and signal processing. Topics include input-output and state-space models of linear systems driven by deterministic and random signals; time- and transform-domain representations in discrete and continuous time; and group delay. State feedback and observers. Probabilistic models; stochastic processes, correlation functions, power spectra, spectral factorization. Least-mean square error estimation; Wiener filtering. Hypothesis testing; detection; matched filters.
<br><I>A. V. Oppenheim, G. C. Verghese</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.012"></a>
<p><h3>6.012 Microelectronic Devices and Circuits
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.002">6.002</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.012"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-141</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>WF1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-302</a>) or <i>WF2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-302</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Microelectronic device modeling, and basic microelectronic circuit analysis and design. Physical electronics of semiconductor junction and MOS devices. Relating terminal behavior to internal physical processes, developing circuit models, and understanding the uses and limitations of different models. Use of incremental and large-signal techniques to analyze and design transistor circuits, with examples chosen from digital circuits, linear amplifiers, and other integrated circuits. Design project.
<br><I>A. I. Akinwande, J. Kong, T. Palacios, C. G. Sodini</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.013"></a>
<p><h3>6.013 Electromagnetics and Applications
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=m2" title="18.02, 18.02A, 18.022, 18.023, 18.024">18.02</a>, <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p2" title="8.02, 8.021, 8.022">8.02</a>
<br>Units: 3-5-4
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Analysis and design of modern applications that employ electromagnetic phenomena for signals and power transmission in RF, microwaves, optical and wireless communication systems. Fundamentals include dynamic solutions for Maxwell's equations; electromagnetic power and energy, waves in media, metallic and dielectric waveguides, radiation, and diffraction; resonance; filters; and acoustic analogs. Labs activities range from building to testing of devices and systems (e.g., antenna arrays, radars, dielectric waveguides). Students work in teams on self-proposed maker-style design projects with a focus on fostering creativity, teamwork, and debugging skills. 6.002, 6003 and 6.007 are recommended but not required.
<br><I>L. Daniel, M. R. Watts</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.02"></a>
<p><h3>6.02 Introduction to EECS via Communications Networks
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.0001">6.0001</a>
<br>Units: 4-4-4
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.02"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-101</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>TR10</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-304</a>) or <i>TR11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-304</a>) or <i>TR12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-304</a>) or <i>TR1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-304</a>) or <i>TR2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-301</a>) or <i>TR3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-301</a>) or <i>TR10</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=35">35-310</a>) or <i>TR11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=35">35-310</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Studies key concepts, systems, and algorithms to reliably communicate data in settings ranging from the cellular phone network and the Internet to deep space. Weekly laboratory experiments explore these areas in depth. Topics presented in three modules - bits, signals, and packets - spanning the multiple layers of a communication system. Bits module includes information, entropy, data compression algorithms, and error correction with block and convolutional codes. Signals module includes modeling physical channels and noise, signal design, filtering and detection, modulation, and frequency-division multiplexing. Packets module includes switching and queuing principles, media access control, routing protocols, and data transport protocols.
<br><I>H. Balakrishnan, K. LaCurts, G. C. Verghese,</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.021"></a>
<p><h3>6.021[J] Cellular Neurophysiology and Computing
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2b.html#2.791">2.791[J]</A>, <A HREF="m9a.html#9.21">9.21[J]</A>, <A HREF="m20a.html#20.370">20.370[J]</A>)<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m2b.html#2.794">2.794[J]</A>, <A HREF="m6b.html#6.521">6.521[J]</A>, <A HREF="m9a.html#9.021">9.021[J]</A>, <A HREF="m20a.html#20.470">20.470[J]</A>, <A HREF="mHSTa.html#HST.541">HST.541[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p2" title="8.02, 8.021, 8.022">8.02</a>; <a href="m18a.html#18.03">18.03</a>; <a href="m2a.html#2.005">2.005</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.002">6.002</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.003">6.003</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.071">6.071</a>, <a href="m10a.html#10.301">10.301</a>, <a href="m20a.html#20.110">20.110</a>, or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 5-2-5
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.021"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW11-12.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-124</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>TBA</i> <b>Recitation:</b> <i>T12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-303</a>) or <i>T4</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-302</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Integrated overview of the biophysics of cells from prokaryotes to neurons, with a focus on mass transport and electrical signal generation across cell membrane. First third of course focuses on mass transport through membranes: diffusion, osmosis, chemically mediated, and active transport. Second third focuses on electrical properties of cells: ion transport to action potential generation and propagation in electrically excitable cells. Synaptic transmission. Electrical properties interpreted via kinetic and molecular properties of single voltage-gated ion channels. Final third focuses on biophysics of synaptic transmission and introduction to neural computing. Laboratory and computer exercises illustrate the concepts. Students taking graduate version complete different assignments. Preference to juniors and seniors.
<br><I>J. Han, T. Heldt</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.022"></a>
<p><h3>6.022[J] Quantitative Systems Physiology
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2b.html#2.792">2.792[J]</A>, <A HREF="mHSTa.html#HST.542">HST.542[J]</A>)<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m2b.html#2.796">2.796[J]</A>, <A HREF="m6b.html#6.522">6.522[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p2" title="8.02, 8.021, 8.022">8.02</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.03">18.03</a>, or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 4-2-6
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/6.022j/www/">http://web.mit.edu/6.022j/www/</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Application of the principles of energy and mass flow to major human organ systems. Mechanisms of regulation and homeostasis. Anatomical, physiological and pathophysiological features of the cardiovascular, respiratory and renal systems. Systems, features and devices that are most illuminated by the methods of physical sciences. Laboratory work includes some animal studies. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.  2 Engineering Design Points.
<br><I>T. Heldt, R. G. Mark, C. M. Stultz</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.023"></a>
<p><h3>6.023[J] Fields, Forces and Flows in Biological Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2b.html#2.793">2.793[J]</A>, <A HREF="m20a.html#20.330">20.330[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p2" title="8.02, 8.021, 8.022">8.02</a>; <a href="m2a.html#2.005">2.005</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.021">6.021</a>, or permission of instructor, <I><a href="m20a.html#20.309">20.309</a></I>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to electric fields, fluid flows, transport phenomena and their application to biological systems. Flux and continuity laws, Maxwell's equations, electro-quasistatics, electro-chemical-mechanical driving forces, conservation of mass and momentum, Navier-Stokes flows, and electrokinetics. Applications include biomolecular transport in tissues, electrophoresis, and microfluidics.
<br><I>J. Han, S. Manalis</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.024"></a>
<p><h3>6.024[J] Molecular, Cellular, and Tissue Biomechanics
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2b.html#2.797">2.797[J]</A>, <A HREF="m3a.html#3.053">3.053[J]</A>, <A HREF="m20a.html#20.310">20.310[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m2b.html#2.370">2.370</a> or <a href="m2b.html#2.772">2.772J</a>; <a href="m18a.html#18.03">18.03</a> or <a href="m3a.html#3.016">3.016</a>; <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=b" title="7.012, 7.013, 7.014, 7.015, 7.016">7.012</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.024"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR1-2.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-163</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Develops and applies scaling laws and the methods of continuum mechanics to biomechanical phenomena over a range of length scales. Topics include structure of tissues and the molecular basis for macroscopic properties; chemical and electrical effects on mechanical behavior; cell mechanics, motility and adhesion; biomembranes; biomolecular mechanics and molecular motors. Experimental methods for probing structures at the tissue, cellular, and molecular levels.
<br><I>R. D. Kamm, A. J. Grodzinsky, K. Van Vliet</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.025"></a>
<p><h3>6.025[J] Medical Device Design
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2b.html#2.750">2.750[J]</A>)<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m2b.html#2.75">2.75[J]</A>, <A HREF="m6b.html#6.525">6.525[J]</A>, <A HREF="mHSTa.html#HST.552">HST.552[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m2b.html#2.70">2.70</a>, <a href="m2b.html#2.72">2.72</a>, <a href="m2b.html#2.678">2.678</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.115">6.115</a>, <a href="m22a.html#22.071">22.071</a>, or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/2.75/">http://web.mit.edu/2.75/</a>
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.025"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW1-2.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=3">3-270</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Application of mechanical and electrical engineering fundamentals to the design of medical devices that address clinical needs. Throughout the term, students work in small teams on a major project to translate a clinical challenge into a proof-of-concept prototype device. Students conduct user analysis, develop design specifications, and follow a structured process to cultivate creative designs and apply analytical techniques to optimize them. They deepen their understanding of art and intellectual property by researching prior representations. Develops practical skills in prototyping and testing as well as project management. Includes lectures, problem sets and exams that focus on design fundamentals. Instruction and practice in written and oral communication provided. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments. Enrollment limited.
<br><I>A. H. Slocum, G. Hom</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.027"></a>
<p><h3>6.027[J] Biomolecular Feedback Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2a.html#2.180">2.180[J]</A>)<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m2a.html#2.18">2.18[J]</A>, <A HREF="m6b.html#6.557">6.557[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m18a.html#18.03">18.03</a>, <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=b" title="7.012, 7.013, 7.014, 7.015, 7.016">7.012</a>, or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Comprehensive introduction to dynamics and control of biomolecular systems with emphasis on design/analysis techniques from control theory. Provides a review of biology concepts, regulation mechanisms, and models. Covers basic enabling technologies, engineering principles for designing biological functions, modular design techniques, and design limitations. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.
<br><I>D. Del Vecchio</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.03"></a>
<p><h3>6.03 Introduction to EECS via Medical Technology
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=m2" title="18.02, 18.02A, 18.022, 18.023, 18.024">18.02</a>, <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p2" title="8.02, 8.021, 8.022">8.02</a>
<br>Units: 4-4-4
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Explores biomedical signals generated from electrocardiograms, glucose detectors or ultrasound images, and magnetic resonance images. Topics include physical characterization and modeling of systems in the time and frequency domains; analog and digital signals and noise; basic machine learning including decision trees, clustering, and classification; and introductory machine vision. Labs designed to strengthen background in signal processing and machine learning. Students design and run structured experiments, and develop and test procedures through further experimentation.
<br><I>C. M. Stultz, E. Adalsteinsson</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.031"></a>
<p><h3>6.031 Elements of Software Construction
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.009">6.009</a>
<br>Units: 5-0-10
<br>URL: <a href="http://mit.edu/6.031">http://mit.edu/6.031</a>
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.031"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MWF11-12.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-101</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces fundamental principles and techniques of software development: how to write software that is safe from bugs, easy to understand, and ready for change. Topics include specifications and invariants; testing, test-case generation, and coverage; abstract data types and representation independence; design patterns for object-oriented programming; concurrent programming, including message passing and shared concurrency, and defending against races and deadlock; and functional programming with immutable data and higher-order functions. Includes weekly programming exercises and larger group programming projects.
<br><I>M. Goldman, R. C. Miller</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.033"></a>
<p><h3>6.033 Computer System Engineering
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.004">6.004</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.009">6.009</a>
<br>Units: 5-1-6
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/6.033">http://web.mit.edu/6.033</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Topics on the engineering of computer software and hardware systems: techniques for controlling complexity; strong modularity using client-server design, operating systems; performance, networks; naming; security and privacy; fault-tolerant systems, atomicity and coordination of concurrent activities, and recovery; impact of computer systems on society.  Case studies of working systems and readings from the current literature provide comparisons and contrasts.  Includes a single, semester-long design project.  Students engage in extensive written communication exercises. Enrollment may be limited.
<br><I>K. LaCurts, M. F. Kaashoek, H. Balakrishnan</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-322</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-301</a>) or <i>T1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=38">38-166</a>) or <i>T3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=38">38-166</a>) or <i>M12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=38">38-166</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-302</a>) or <i>T11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=26">26-302</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces representations, methods, and architectures used to build applications and to account for human intelligence from a computational point of view. Covers applications of rule chaining, constraint propagation, constrained search, inheritance, statistical inference, and other problem-solving paradigms. Also addresses applications of identification trees, neural nets, genetic algorithms, support-vector machines, boosting, and other learning paradigms. Considers what separates human intelligence from that of other animals.
<br><I>P. H. Winston</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->

<a name="6.042"></a>
<p><h3>6.042[J] Mathematics for Computer Science
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/rest.gif" alt="Rest Elec in Sci & Tech" title="Rest Elec in Sci & Tech" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m18a.html#18.062">18.062[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=m1" title="18.01, 18.01A, 18.014">18.01</a>
<br>Units: 5-0-7
<br>URL: <a href="http://theory.csail.mit.edu/classes/6.042">http://theory.csail.mit.edu/classes/6.042</a>
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.042"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MWF1-2.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-044</a>) or <i>MWF2.30-4</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-044</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-082</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Elementary discrete mathematics for computer science and engineering. Emphasis on mathematical definitions and proofs as well as on applicable methods.  Topics include formal logic notation, proof methods; induction, well-ordering; sets, relations; elementary graph theory; asymptotic notation and growth of functions; permutations and combinations, counting principles; discrete probability.  Further selected topics include recursive definition and structural induction, state machines and invariants, integer congruences, recurrences, generating functions.
<br><I>F. T. Leighton, A. R. Meyer, A. Moitra</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.045"></a>
<p><h3>6.045[J] Automata, Computability, and Complexity
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m18a.html#18.400">18.400[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.042">6.042</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br>URL: <a href="http://math.mit.edu/classes/18.400">http://math.mit.edu/classes/18.400</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Mathematical introduction to questions concerning the definition of computation, and what problems can be solved by computers. Considers what problems can be efficiently solved by way of finite automata, circuits, Turing machines, and communication complexity. Provides complete, rigorous answers to the questions in some cases; others are major open problems. Builds skills in classifying computational problems in terms of their difficulty. Discusses other fundamental issues, including the Church-Turing Thesis, the P versus NP problem, and the power of randomness.
<br><I>R. Williams</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.046"></a>
<p><h3>6.046[J] Design and Analysis of Algorithms
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m18a.html#18.410">18.410[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.006">6.006</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br>URL: <a href="http://math.mit.edu/classes/18.410">http://math.mit.edu/classes/18.410</a>
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.046"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR11-12.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-123</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>F10</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-149</a>) or <i>F11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-159</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-149</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=36">36-156</a>) or <i>F12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=36">36-156</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-159</a>) or <i>F1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-159</a>, <a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-149</a>) or <i>F2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=35">35-308</a>) or <i>F3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=35">35-308</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Techniques for the design and analysis of efficient algorithms, emphasizing methods useful in practice. Topics include sorting; search trees, heaps, and hashing; divide-and-conquer; dynamic programming; greedy algorithms; amortized analysis; graph algorithms; and shortest paths. Advanced topics may include network flow; computational geometry; number-theoretic algorithms; polynomial and matrix calculations; caching; and parallel computing.
<br><I>E. Demaine, M. Goemans</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.047"></a>
<p><h3>6.047 Computational Biology: Genomes, Networks, Evolution
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6c.html#6.878">6.878[J]</A>, <A HREF="mHSTa.html#HST.507">HST.507[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.006">6.006</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.041B">6.041B</a>, <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=b" title="7.012, 7.013, 7.014, 7.015, 7.016">7.012</a>; or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.047"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR1-2.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-141</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>F3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-237</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Covers the algorithmic and machine learning foundations of computational biology, combining theory with practice. Principles of algorithm design, influential problems and techniques, and analysis of large-scale biological datasets. Topics include (a) genomes: sequence analysis, gene finding, RNA folding, genome alignment and assembly, database search; (b) networks: gene expression analysis, regulatory motifs, biological network analysis; (c) evolution: comparative genomics, phylogenetics, genome duplication, genome rearrangements, evolutionary theory.  These are coupled with fundamental algorithmic techniques including: dynamic programming, hashing, Gibbs sampling, expectation maximization, hidden Markov models, stochastic context-free grammars, graph clustering, dimensionality reduction, Bayesian networks.
<br><I>M. Kellis</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.049"></a>
<p><h3>6.049[J] Evolutionary Biology:  Concepts, Models and Computation
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m7a.html#7.33">7.33[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m7a.html#7.03">7.03</a>; <a href="m6a.html#6.0001">6.0001</a> or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Explores and illustrates how evolution explains biology, with an emphasis on computational model building for analyzing evolutionary data.  Covers key concepts of biological evolution, including adaptive evolution, neutral evolution, evolution of sex, genomic conflict, speciation, phylogeny and comparative methods, life's history, coevolution, human evolution, and evolution of disease.
<br><I>R. Berwick, D. Bartel</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.050"></a>
<p><h3>6.050[J] Information, Entropy, and Computation
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2a.html#2.110">2.110[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p1" title="8.01, 8.01L, 8.011, 8.012">8.01</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-6
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Explores the ultimate limits to communication and computation, with an emphasis on the physical nature of information and information processing. Topics include information and computation, digital signals, codes, and compression. Biological representations of information. Logic circuits, computer architectures, and algorithmic information. Noise, probability, and error correction. The concept of entropy applied to channel capacity and to the second law of thermodynamics. Reversible and irreversible operations and the physics of computation. Quantum computation.
<br><I>S. Lloyd, P. Penfield, Jr.</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<p><h3>6.061 Introduction to Electric Power Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>

<p><h3>6.070[J] Electronics Project Laboratory
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)

<p><h3>6.072[J] Introduction to Digital Electronics
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="mECa.html#EC.110">EC.110[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 0-3-3 [P/D/F]
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.072"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>M EVE (7-10 PM)</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-402</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Design your own circuits for times when off-the-shelf solutions are not available. Seminar begins with assembly of a utility board. Weekly labs cover digital logic gates, memory elements, and finite-state machine design. Seminar concludes with a team-based design project. Preference given to freshmen. Maximum of 10 students per term, lottery at the first class session if oversubscribed .
<br><I>J. Bales</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.073"></a>
<p><h3>6.073[J] Creating Video Games
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/hassA.gif" alt="HASS Arts" title="HASS Arts" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="mCMSa.html#CMS.611">CMS.611[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.01">6.01</a>, <a href="mCMSa.html#CMS.301">CMS.301</a>, or <a href="mCMSa.html#CMS.608">CMS.608</a>
<br>Units: 3-3-6
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces students to the complexities of working in small, multidisciplinary teams to develop video games. Covers creative design and production methods, stressing design iteration and regular testing across all aspects of game development (design, visual arts, music, fiction, and programming). Assumes a familiarity with current video games, and the ability to discuss games critically. Previous experience in audio design, visual arts, or project management recommended. Limited to 24.
<br><I>P. Tan, S. Verrilli, R. Eberhardt</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<a name="6.S08"></a>
<p><h3>6.S08 Special Subject: Introduction to EECS via Interconnected Embedded Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: None. <I><a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p2" title="8.02, 8.021, 8.022">8.02</a></I>
<br>Units: 1-5-6
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to embedded systems in the context of connected devices, wearables and the "Internet of Things" (IoT). Topics include microcontrollers, energy utilization, algorithmic efficiency, interfacing with sensors, networking, cryptography, and local versus distributed computation. Students design, make, and program an internet-connected wearable or handheld device. In final project, student teams design and demo their own cloud-connected IoT system. Licensed for Spring 2017 by the Committee on Curricula. Enrollment limited; preference to first- and second-year students.
<br><I>J. Voldman, J. D. Steinmeyer</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<h2>Undergraduate Laboratory Subjects</h2>
<a name="6.100"></a>
<p><h3>6.100 Electrical Engineering and Computer Science Project
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Summer" title="Summer" src="/icns/summer.gif">) <img src="/icns/repeat.gif" alt="Can be repeated for credit" title="Can be repeated for credit" width=16 height=16 align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units arranged
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.100"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> TBA. <!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Individual experimental work related to electrical engineering and computer science. Student must make arrangements with a project supervisor and file a proposal endorsed by the supervisor. Departmental approval required. Written report to be submitted upon completion of work.
<br>Consult Department Undergraduate Office<br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.101"></a>
<p><h3>6.101 Introductory Analog Electronics Laboratory
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.002">6.002</a> or <a href="m6a.html#6.071">6.071</a>
<br>Units: 2-9-1
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/6.101/www/index.html">http://web.mit.edu/6.101/www/index.html</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introductory experimental laboratory explores the design, construction, and debugging of analog electronic circuits. Lectures and laboratory projects in the first half of the course investigate the performance characteristics of semiconductor devices (diodes, BJTs, and MOSFETs) and functional analog building blocks, including single-stage amplifiers, op amps, small audio amplifier, filters, converters, sensor circuits, and medical electronics (ECG, pulse-oximetry). Projects involve design, implementation, and presentation in an environment similar to that of industry engineering design teams. Instruction and practice in written and oral communication provided. Opportunity to simulate real-world problems and solutions that involve tradeoffs and the use of engineering judgment.
<br><I>G. Hom</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.111"></a>
<p><h3>6.111 Introductory Digital Systems Laboratory
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.002">6.002</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.071">6.071</a>, or <a href="m16a.html#16.004">16.004</a>
<br>Units: 3-7-2
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.111"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR2.30-4</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-141</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>TBA</i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Lectures and labs on digital logic, flip flops, PALs, FPGAs, counters, timing, synchronization, and finite-state machines prepare students for the design and implementation of a final project of their choice: games, music, digital filters, wireless communications, video, or graphics. Extensive use of Verilog for describing and implementing digital logic designs.
<br><I>G. P. Hom, A. P. Chandrakasan</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.115"></a>
<p><h3>6.115 Microcomputer Project Laboratory
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6a.html#6.1151">6.1151</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.002">6.002</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.003">6.003</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.004">6.004</a>, or <a href="m6a.html#6.007">6.007</a>
<br>Units: 3-6-3
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces analysis and design of embedded systems. Microcontrollers provide adaptation, flexibility, and real-time control. Emphasizes construction of complete systems, including a five-axis robot arm, a fluorescent lamp ballast, a tomographic imaging station (e.g., a CAT scan), and a simple calculator. Presents a wide range of basic tools, including software and development tools, programmable system on chip, peripheral components such as A/D converters, communication schemes, signal processing techniques, closed-loop digital feedback control, interface and power electronics, and modeling of electromechanical systems. Includes a sequence of assigned projects, followed by a final project of the student's choice, emphasizing creativity and uniqueness. Provides instruction in written and oral communication. To satisfy the independent inquiry component of this subject, students expand the scope of their laboratory project.
<br><I>S. B. Leeb</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<a name="6.117"></a>
<p><h3>6.117 Introduction to Electrical Engineering Lab Skills
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="IAP" title="IAP" src="/icns/iap.gif">)
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 1-3-2 [P/D/F]
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces basic electrical engineering concepts, components, and laboratory techniques. Covers analog integrated circuits, power supplies, and digital circuits. Lab exercises provide practical experience in constructing projects using multi-meters, oscilloscopes, logic analyzers, and other tools. Includes a project in which students build a circuit to display their own EKG. Enrollment limited.
<br><I>G. P. Hom</I><br>

<a name="6.123"></a>
<p><h3>6.123[J] Bioinstrumentation Project Lab
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m20a.html#20.345">20.345[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=b" title="7.012, 7.013, 7.014, 7.015, 7.016">7.012</a>, and <a href="m2a.html#2.004">2.004</a> or <a href="m6a.html#6.003">6.003</a>; or <a href="m20a.html#20.309">20.309</a>; or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 2-7-3
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>In-depth examination of instrumentation design, principles and techniques for studying biological systems, from single molecules to entire organisms. Lectures cover optics, advanced microscopy techniques, electronics for biological measurement, magnetic resonance imaging, computed tomography, MEMs, microfluidic devices, and limits of detection. Students select two lab exercises during the first half of the semester and complete a final design project in the second half. Lab emphasizes design process and skillful realization of a robust system. Enrollment limited; preference to Course 20 majors and minors.
<br><I>E. Boyden, M. Jonas, S. F. Nagle, P. So, S. Wasserman, M. F. Yanik</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.129"></a>
<p><h3>6.129[J] Biological Circuit Engineering Laboratory
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m20a.html#20.129">20.129[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=b" title="7.012, 7.013, 7.014, 7.015, 7.016">7.012</a>, <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=m2" title="18.02, 18.02A, 18.022, 18.023, 18.024">18.02</a>
<br>Units: 2-8-2
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Students assemble individual genes and regulatory elements into larger-scale circuits; they experimentally characterize these circuits in yeast cells using quantitative techniques, including flow cytometry, and model their results computationally. Emphasizes concepts and techniques to perform independent experimental and computational synthetic biology research. Discusses current literature and ongoing research in the field of synthetic biology. Instruction and practice in oral and written communication provided. Enrollment limited.
<br><I>T. Lu, R. Weiss</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.131"></a>
<p><h3>6.131 Power Electronics Laboratory
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6a.html#6.1311">6.1311</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.002">6.002</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.003">6.003</a>, or <a href="m6a.html#6.007">6.007</a>
<br>Units: 3-6-3
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.131"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-101</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>W3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-101</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces the design and construction of power electronic circuits and motor drives.  Laboratory exercises include the construction of drive circuitry for an electric go-cart, flash strobes, computer power supplies, three-phase inverters for AC motors, and resonant drives for lamp ballasts and induction heating. Basic electric machines introduced include DC, induction, and permanent magnet motors, with drive considerations. Provides instruction in written and oral communication. Students taking independent inquiry version 6.1131 expand the scope of their laboratory project.
<br><I>S. B. Leeb</I><br><a href="javascript:PopUpHelp('http://eduapps.mit.edu/textbook/books.html?Term=2018FA&Subject=6.131');" >Textbooks (Fall 2017)</a></font>

<a name="6.141"></a>
<p><h3>6.141[J] Robotics: Science and Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m16a.html#16.405">16.405[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m1a.html#1.00">1.00</a> or <a href="m6a.html#6.0001">6.0001</a>; <a href="m2a.html#2.003">2.003</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.006">6.006</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.009">6.009</a>, or <a href="m16a.html#16.06">16.06</a>; or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 2-6-4
<br>URL: <a href="http://courses.csail.mit.edu/rss/">http://courses.csail.mit.edu/rss/</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Presents concepts, principles, and algorithms for sensing and computation related to the physical world. Topics include motion planning, geometric reasoning, kinematics and dynamics, state estimation, tracking, map building, manipulation, human-robot interaction, fault diagnosis, and embedded system development. Students specify and design a small-scale yet complex robot capable of real-time interaction with the natural world. Students engage in extensive written and oral communication exercises. Enrollment limited.
<br><I>S. Karaman, D. Rus</I><br>
<a name="6.146"></a>
<p><h3>6.146 Mobile Autonomous Systems Laboratory: MASLAB
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="IAP" title="IAP" src="/icns/iap.gif">) <img src="/icns/repeat.gif" alt="Can be repeated for credit" title="Can be repeated for credit" width=16 height=16 align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 2-2-2 [P/D/F]
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Autonomous robotics contest emphasizing technical AI, vision, mapping and navigation from a robot-mounted camera. Few restrictions are placed on materials, sensors, and/or actuators enabling teams to build robots very creatively. Teams should have members with varying engineering, programming and mechanical backgrounds. Culminates with a robot competition at the end of IAP. Enrollment limited.
<br><I>Staff</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.147"></a>
<p><h3>6.147 The Battlecode Programming Competition
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>

<br>Artificial Intelligence programming contest in Java. Student teams program virtual robots to play Battlecode, a real-time strategy game. Competition culminates in a live BattleCode tournament. Assumes basic knowledge of programming.

<a name="6.150"></a>
<p><h3>6.150 Mobile Applications Competition
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="IAP" title="IAP" src="/icns/iap.gif">) <img src="/icns/repeat.gif" alt="Can be repeated for credit" title="Can be repeated for credit" width=16 height=16 align="bottom"><br>Not offered regularly; consult department

<a name="6.151"></a>
<p><h3>6.151 iOS Game Design and Development Competition
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="IAP" title="IAP" src="/icns/iap.gif">)
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 2-2-2 [P/D/F]
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to iOS game design and development for students already familiar with object-oriented programming. Provides a set of basic tools (Objective-C and Cocos2D) and exposure to real-world issues in game design. Working in small teams, students complete a final project in which they create their own iPhone game. At the end of IAP, teams present their games in competition for prizes awarded by a judging panel of gaming experts.
<br><I>Staff</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.152"></a>
<p><h3>6.152[J] Micro/Nano Processing Technology
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m3a.html#3.155">3.155[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=m2" title="18.02, 18.02A, 18.022, 18.023, 18.024">18.02</a>, <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=c" title="3.091, 5.111, 5.112">5.111</a>, <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p2" title="8.02, 8.021, 8.022">8.02</a>, or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-4-5
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.152"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW2.30-4</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-124</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces the theory and technology of micro/nano fabrication. Includes lectures and laboratory sessions on basic processing techniques such as vacuum processes, lithography, diffusion, oxidation, and pattern transfer. Students fabricate solar cells, MEMS cantilevers, and microfluidic mixers. Emphasizes interrelationships between material properties and processing, device structure, and the electrical, mechanical, optical, chemical  or biological behavior of devices. Provides background for thesis work in micro/nano fabrication. Students engage in extensive written and oral communication exercises.
<br><I>L. F. Velasquez-Garcia, J. Michel</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.161"></a>
<p><h3>6.161 Modern Optics Project Laboratory
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6b.html#6.637">6.637</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.003">6.003</a>
<br>Units: 3-5-4
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/6.161/www/index.html">http://web.mit.edu/6.161/www/index.html</a>
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.161"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR2.30-4</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-304</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>TBA</i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Lectures, laboratory exercises and projects on optical signal generation, transmission, detection, storage, processing and display. Topics include polarization properties of light; reflection and refraction; coherence and interference; Fraunhofer and Fresnel diffraction; holography; Fourier optics; coherent and incoherent imaging and signal processing systems; optical properties of materials; lasers and LEDs; electro-optic and acousto-optic light modulators; photorefractive and liquid-crystal light modulation; display technologies; optical waveguides and fiber-optic communication systems; photodetectors. Students may use this subject to find an advanced undergraduate project. Students engage in extensive oral and written communcation exercises. Recommended prerequisites: 6.007 or 8.03.
<br><I>C. Warde</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.163"></a>
<p><h3>6.163 Strobe Project Laboratory
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p2" title="8.02, 8.021, 8.022">8.02</a> or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 2-8-2
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.163"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=1">1-134</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>TBA</i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Application of electronic flash sources to measurement and   photography. First half covers fundamentals of photography and   electronic flashes, including experiments on application of electronic   flash to photography, stroboscopy, motion analysis, and high-speed   videography. Students write four extensive lab reports.  In the second half, students work in small groups to select, design,   and execute independent projects in measurement or photography that apply learned techniques. Project planning and execution skills are discussed and developed over the term.  Students engage in extensive written and oral communication exercises. Enrollment limited.
<br><I>J. K. Vandiver, J. W. Bales</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->

<a name="6.172"></a>
<p><h3>6.172 Performance Engineering of Software Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6c.html#6.871">6.871</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.004">6.004</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.006">6.006</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.031">6.031</a>
<br>Units: 3-12-3
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.172"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR2.30-4</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-101</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>F10-12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-265</a>) or <i>F1-3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-265</a>) or <i>F3-5</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-265</a>) or <i>F10-12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=24">24-307</a>) or <i>F1-3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-301</a>) or <i>F3-5</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-301</a>) or <i>F2-4</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-304</a>) or <i>F3-5</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=36">36-155</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Project-based introduction to building efficient, high-performance and scalable software systems. Topics include performance analysis, algorithmic techniques for high performance, instruction-level optimizations, vectorization, cache and memory hierarchy optimization, and parallel programming. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.
<br><I>S. Amarasinghe, C. E. Leiserson</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.175"></a>
<p><h3>6.175 Constructive Computer Architecture
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.004">6.004</a>
<br>Units: 3-8-1
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.175"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MWF3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-302</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Illustrates a constructive (as opposed to a descriptive) approach to computer architecture. Topics include combinational and pipelined arithmetic-logic units (ALU), in-order pipelined microarchitectures, branch prediction, blocking and unblocking caches, interrupts, virtual memory support, cache coherence and multicore architectures. Labs in a modern Hardware Design Language (HDL) illustrate various aspects of microprocessor design, culminating in a term project in which students present a multicore design running on an FPGA board.
<br><I>Arvind</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
