<a name="6.182"></a>
<p><h3>6.182 Psychoacoustics Project Laboratory
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/Lab.gif" alt="Institute Lab" title="Institute Lab" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 3-6-3
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces the methods used to measure human auditory abilities. Discusses auditory function, principles of psychoacoustic measurement, models for psychoacoustic performance, and experimental techniques. Project topics: absolute and differential auditory sensitivity, operating characteristics of human observers, span of auditory judgment, adaptive measurement procedures, and scaling sensory magnitudes. Knowledge of probability helpful. Students engage in extensive written and oral communication exercises.
<br><I>L. D. Braida</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<h2>Senior Projects</h2>
<a name="6.UAP"></a>
<p><h3>6.UAP Undergraduate Advanced Project
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>

<a name="6.UAR"></a>
<p><h3>6.UAR Seminar in Undergraduate Advanced Research
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/repeat.gif" alt="Can be repeated for credit" title="Can be repeated for credit" width=16 height=16 align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6c.html#6.UR">6.UR</a>, permission of instructor
<br>Units: 2-0-4
<br>URL: <a href="https://superurop.eecs.mit.edu/">https://superurop.eecs.mit.edu/</a>
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.UAR"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>R4</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-123</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Instruction in effective undergraduate research, including choosing and developing a research topic, surveying previous work and publications, research topics in EECS, industry best practices, design for robustness, technical presentation, authorship and collaboration, and ethics.  Students engage in extensive written and oral communication exercises, in the context of an approved advanced research project. A total of 12 units of credit is awarded for completion of the Fall and subsequent Spring term offerings. Application required; consult EECS SuperUROP website for more information.
<br><I>A. P. Chandrakasan, D. M. Freeman, D. Katabi</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->

<h2>Advanced Undergraduate Subjects and Graduate Subjects by Area</h2>
<h3>Systems Science and Control Engineering</h3>
<a name="6.207"></a>
<p><h3>6.207[J] Networks
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/hassS.gif" alt="HASS Social Sciences" title="HASS Social Sciences" width="16" height="16" align="bottom">
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m14a.html#14.15">14.15[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.041B">6.041B</a> or <a href="m14a.html#14.30">14.30</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Highlights common principles that permeate the functioning of diverse technological, economic and social networks. Utilizes three sets of tools for analyzing networks--random graph models, optimization, and game theory--to study informational and learning cascades; economic and financial networks; social influence networks; formation of social groups; communication networks and the Internet; consensus and gossiping; spread and control of epidemics; control and use of energy networks; and biological networks.
<br><I>D. Shah, A. Teytelboym</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.215"></a>
<p><h3>6.215 Optimization Methods
<br>(New)
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6a.html#6.255">6.255[J]</A>, <A HREF="m15a.html#15.093">15.093[J]</A>, <A HREF="mIDSa.html#IDS.200">IDS.200[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.215"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> TBA. <!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces the principal algorithms for linear, network, discrete, robust, nonlinear, and dynamic optimization. Emphasizes methodology and the underlying mathematical structures. Topics include the simplex method, network flow methods, branch and bound and cutting plane methods for discrete optimization, optimality conditions for nonlinear optimization, interior point methods for convex optimization, Newton's method, heuristic methods, and dynamic programming and optimal control methods. Expectations and evaluation criteria differ for students taking graduate version; consult syllabus or instructor for specific details.
<br><I>D. Bertsimas, P. Parrilo</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.231"></a>
<p><h3>6.231 Dynamic Programming and Stochastic Control
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.041B">6.041B</a> or <a href="m18b.html#18.600">18.600</a>; <a href="m18a.html#18.100A">18.100A</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.100B">18.100B</a>, or <a href="m18a.html#18.100Q">18.100Q</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/6.231/www/6231.html">http://web.mit.edu/6.231/www/6231.html</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Sequential decision-making via dynamic programming. Unified approach to optimal control of stochastic dynamic systems and Markovian decision problems. Applications in linear-quadratic control, inventory control, resource allocation, scheduling, and planning. Optimal decision making under perfect and imperfect state information. Certainty equivalent, open loop-feedback control, rollout, model predictive control, aggregation, and other suboptimal control methods. Infinite horizon problems: discounted, stochastic shortest path, average cost, and semi-Markov models. Value and policy iteration. Abstract models in dynamic programming. Approximate/neurodynamic programming. Simulation based methods. Discussion of current research on the solution of large-scale problems.
<br><I>J. N. Tsitsiklis</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.241"></a>
<p><h3>6.241[J] Dynamic Systems and Control
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m16a.html#16.338">16.338[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.003">6.003</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Linear, discrete- and continuous-time, multi-input-output systems in control, related areas. Least squares and matrix perturbation problems. State-space models, modes, stability, controllability, observability, transfer function matrices, poles and zeros, and minimality. Internal stability of interconnected systems, feedback compensators, state feedback, optimal regulation, observers, and observer-based compensators. Measures of control performance, robustness issues using singular values of transfer functions. Introductory ideas on nonlinear systems. Recommended prerequisite: 6.302.
<br><I>M. A. Dahleh, A. Megretski</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.245"></a>
<p><h3>6.245 Multivariable Control Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.241">6.241</a> or <a href="m16a.html#16.31">16.31</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/6.245/www/index.html">http://web.mit.edu/6.245/www/index.html</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Computer-aided design methodologies for synthesis of multivariable feedback control systems. Performance and robustness trade-offs. Model-based compensators; Q-parameterization; ill-posed optimization problems; dynamic augmentation; linear-quadratic optimization of controllers; H-infinity controller design; Mu-synthesis; model and compensator simplification; nonlinear effects. Computer-aided (MATLAB) design homework using models of physical processes.
<br><I>A. Megretski</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<a name="6.251"></a>
<p><h3>6.251[J] Introduction to Mathematical Programming
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m15a.html#15.081">15.081[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.251"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR1-2.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-155</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>F10</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=36">36-156</a>) or <i>F12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-144</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to linear optimization and its extensions emphasizing both methodology and the underlying mathematical structures and geometrical ideas. Covers classical theory of linear programming as well as some recent advances in the field. Topics: simplex method; duality theory; sensitivity analysis; network flow problems; decomposition; integer programming; interior point algorithms for linear programming; and introduction to combinatorial optimization and NP-completeness.
<br><I>J. N. Tsitsiklis, D. Bertsimas</I><br><a href="javascript:PopUpHelp('http://eduapps.mit.edu/textbook/books.html?Term=2018FA&Subject=6.251');" >Textbooks (Fall 2017)</a></font>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.252"></a>
<p><h3>6.252[J] Nonlinear Optimization
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m15a.html#15.084">15.084[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>; <a href="m18a.html#18.100A">18.100A</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.100B">18.100B</a>, or <a href="m18a.html#18.100C">18.100C</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Unified analytical and computational approach to nonlinear optimization problems. Unconstrained optimization methods include gradient, conjugate direction, Newton, sub-gradient and first-order methods. Constrained optimization methods include feasible directions, projection, interior point methods, and Lagrange multiplier methods. Convex analysis, Lagrangian relaxation, nondifferentiable optimization, and applications in integer programming. Comprehensive treatment of optimality conditions and Lagrange multipliers. Geometric approach to duality theory. Applications drawn from control, communications, power systems, and resource allocation problems.
<br><I>R. M. Freund, P. Parrilo, G. Perakis</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.254"></a>
<p><h3>6.254 Game Theory with Engineering Applications
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.041B">6.041B</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to fundamentals of game theory and mechanism design with motivations for each topic drawn from engineering applications (including distributed control of wireline/wireless communication networks, transportation networks, pricing). Emphasis on the foundations of the theory, mathematical tools, as well as modeling and the equilibrium notion in different environments. Topics include normal form games, supermodular games, dynamic games, repeated games, games with incomplete/imperfect information, mechanism design, cooperative game theory, and network games.
<br><I>A. Ozdaglar</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.255"></a>
<p><h3>6.255[J] Optimization Methods
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m15a.html#15.093">15.093[J]</A>, <A HREF="mIDSa.html#IDS.200">IDS.200[J]</A>)<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6a.html#6.215">6.215</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.255"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR2.30-4</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-123</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>W3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=3">3-333</a>) or <i>F1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=56">56-114</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces the principal algorithms for linear, network, discrete, robust, nonlinear, and dynamic optimization. Emphasizes methodology and the underlying mathematical structures. Topics include the simplex method, network flow methods, branch and bound and cutting plane methods for discrete optimization, optimality conditions for nonlinear optimization, interior point methods for convex optimization, Newton's method, heuristic methods, and dynamic programming and optimal control methods. Expectations and evaluation criteria differ for students taking graduate version; consult syllabus or instructor for specific details.
<br><I>D. Bertsimas, P. Parrilo</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.256"></a>
<p><h3>6.256 Algebraic Techniques and Semidefinite Optimization
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2018-2019" title="Not offered academic year 2018-2019" src="/icns/nonext.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.251">6.251</a> or <a href="m6a.html#6.255">6.255</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Theory and computational techniques for optimization problems involving polynomial equations and inequalities with particular, emphasis on the connections with semidefinite optimization. Develops algebraic and numerical approaches of general applicability, with a view towards methods that simultaneously incorporate both elements, stressing convexity-based ideas, complexity results, and efficient implementations. Examples from several engineering areas, in particular systems and control applications. Topics include semidefinite programming, resultants/discriminants, hyperbolic polynomials, Groebner bases, quantifier elimination, and sum of squares.
<br><I>P. Parrilo</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<a name="6.262"></a>
<p><h3>6.262 Discrete Stochastic Processes
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.041B">6.041B</a>, <a href="m6b.html#6.431B">6.431B</a> or <a href="m18a.html#18.204">18.204</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Review of probability and laws of large numbers; Poisson counting process and renewal processes; Markov chains (including Markov decision theory), branching processes, birth-death processes, and semi-Markov processes; continuous-time Markov chains and reversibility; random walks, martingales, and large deviations; applications from queueing, communication, control, and operations research.
<br><I>R. G. Gallager, V. W. S. Chan</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.263"></a>
<p><h3>6.263[J] Data-Communication Networks
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m16a.html#16.37">16.37[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.041B">6.041B</a> or <a href="m18a.html#18.204">18.204</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Provides an introduction to data networks with an analytic perspective, using  telephone networks, wireless networks, optical networks, the Internet and data centers as primary applications. Presents basic tools for modeling and performance analysis accompanied by elementary, meaningful simulations. Develops insights for large networks by means of simple approximations. Draws upon concepts from queueing theory and optimization.
<br><I>E. Modiano</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.265"></a>
<p><h3>6.265[J] Advanced Stochastic Processes
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m15a.html#15.070">15.070[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6b.html#6.431B">6.431B</a>, <a href="m15a.html#15.085">15.085J</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.100A">18.100A</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.100B">18.100B</a>, or <a href="m18a.html#18.100Q">18.100Q</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Analysis and modeling of stochastic processes. Topics include measure theoretic probability, martingales, filtration, and stopping theorems; elements of large deviations theory; Brownian motion and reflected Brownian motion; stochastic integration and Ito calculus; functional limit theorems. Applications to finance theory, insurance, queueing and inventory models.
<br><I>D. Gamarnik, G. Bresler</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.267"></a>
<p><h3>6.267 Heterogeneous Networks: Architecture, Transport, Proctocols, and Management
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2018-2019" title="Not offered academic year 2018-2019" src="/icns/nonext.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.041B">6.041B</a> or <a href="m6a.html#6.042">6.042</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.267"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW9.30-11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-303</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>F9.30-11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-303</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to modern heterogeneous networks and the provision of heterogeneous services. Architectural principles, analysis, algorithmic techniques, performance analysis, and existing designs are developed and applied to understand current problems in network design and architecture. Begins with basic principles of networking. Emphasizes development of mathematical and algorithmic tools; applies them to understanding network layer design from the performance and scalability viewpoint. Concludes with network management and control, including the architecture and performance analysis of interconnected heterogeneous networks. Provides background and insight to understand current network literature and to perform research on networks with the aid of network design projects.
<br><I>V. W. S. Chan, R. G. Gallager</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.268"></a>
<p><h3>6.268 Network Science and Models
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.041B">6.041B</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces the main mathematical models used to describe large networks and dynamical processes that evolve on networks. Static models of random graphs, preferential attachment, and other graph evolution models.  Epidemic propagation, opinion dynamics, social learning, and inference in networks. Applications drawn from social, economic, natural, and infrastructure networks, as well as networked decision systems such as sensor networks.
<br><I>P. Jaillet, J. N. Tsitsiklis</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<a name="6.301"></a>
<p><h3>6.301 Solid-State Circuits
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.012">6.012</a>
<br>Units: 3-2-7
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/6.301/www/">http://web.mit.edu/6.301/www/</a>
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.301"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR1-2.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-231</a>)<!--s-->

<a name="6.302"></a>
<p><h3>6.302 Feedback System Design
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6b.html#6.320">6.320</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.003">6.003</a>, <a href="m2a.html#2.003">2.003</a>, or <a href="m16a.html#16.002">16.002</a>
<br>Units: 4-3-5
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/6.302/www/">http://web.mit.edu/6.302/www/</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Learn-by-design introduction to continuous and discrete-time system modeling and feedback control. Topics include performance metrics; time- and frequency-domain model extraction: classical control topics, such as dominant pole, PID, and lead-lag compensation; and state-space control topics, such as eigenvalue assignment, linear-quadratic regulators, and observer systems. In lab, students combine circuits, sensors, actuators, algorithms, and a high-performance micro-controller to address problems such as controlling the angle of a propeller-levitated robot arm, stabilizing magnetic levitation, accelerating scans in a tilted-mirror laser imager, eliminating interference in a PWM-based audio amplifier, balancing a two-wheel vehicle, or multi-axis positioning.
<br><I>J. D. Steinmeyer, J. K. White</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<a name="6.334"></a>
<p><h3>6.334 Power Electronics
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.012">6.012</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/course/6/6.334/">http://web.mit.edu/course/6/6.334/</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>The application of electronics to energy conversion and control.  Modeling, analysis, and control techniques.  Design of power circuits including inverters, rectifiers, and dc-dc converters.  Analysis and design of magnetic components and filters.  Characteristics of power semiconductor devices.  Numerous application examples, such as motion control systems, power supplies, and radio-frequency power amplifiers.
<br><I>D. J. Perreault</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.335"></a>
<p><h3>6.335[J] Fast Methods for Partial Differential and Integral Equations
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m18a.html#18.336">18.336[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6b.html#6.336">6.336</a>, <a href="m16b.html#16.920">16.920</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.085">18.085</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.335">18.335</a>, or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.335"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR1-2.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=2">2-143</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Unified introduction to the theory and practice of modern, near linear-time, numerical methods for large-scale partial-differential and integral equations. Topics include preconditioned iterative methods; generalized Fast Fourier Transform and other butterfly-based methods; multiresolution approaches, such as multigrid algorithms and hierarchical low-rank matrix decompositions; and low and high frequency Fast Multipole Methods. Example applications include aircraft design, cardiovascular system modeling, electronic structure computation, and tomographic imaging.
<br><I>C. Perez-Arancibia</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.336"></a>
<p><h3>6.336[J] Introduction to Numerical Simulation
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2a.html#2.096">2.096[J]</A>, <A HREF="m16b.html#16.910">16.910[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m18a.html#18.03">18.03</a> or <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>
<br>Units: 3-3-6
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.336"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW1-2.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-155</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to computational techniques for the simulation of a large variety of engineering and physical systems. Applications are drawn from aerospace, mechanical, electrical, chemical engineering, biology, and materials science. Topics include mathematical formulations (techniques for automatic assembly of mathematical problems from physics' principles); sparse, direct and iterative solution techniques for linear systems; Newton and Homotopy methods for nonlinear problems; discretization methods for ordinary, time-periodic and partial differential equations; accelerated methods for integral equations; techniques for automatic generation of compact dynamical system models and model order reduction.
<br><I>L. Daniel, J. K. White</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.337"></a>
<p><h3>6.337[J] Introduction to Numerical Methods
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m18a.html#18.335">18.335[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>, <a href="m18b.html#18.700">18.700</a>, or <a href="m18b.html#18.701">18.701</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br>URL: <a href="http://math.mit.edu/classes/18.335">http://math.mit.edu/classes/18.335</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Advanced introduction to numerical analysis. Surveys major topics that arise at various levels of solving classic numerical problems, such as systems of linear equations, eigenvalue equations, and least squares problems. Specific topics include matrix factorizations (QR, SVD, LU, Cholesky); direct and iterative methods to solve linear systems (Gaussian elimination, Krylov subspace methods); numerical algorithms to solve eigenvalue equations (Rayleigh quotient iteration, inverse iteration, QR algorithm); conditioning of problems and stability of algorithms; and floating point arithmetic.
<br><I>W. Shin</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.338"></a>
<p><h3>6.338[J] Numerical Computing and Interactive Software
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>

<br>Units: 3-0-9

Provides direct experience with the modern realities of programming supercomputers, GPUs, and multicores in a high-level language.
<br><I>A. Edelman</I><br>No textbook information available

<a name="6.339"></a>
<p><h3>6.339[J] Numerical Methods for Partial Differential Equations
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2a.html#2.097">2.097[J]</A>, <A HREF="m16b.html#16.920">16.920[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m18a.html#18.03">18.03</a> or <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.339"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW9.30-11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-163</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Covers the fundamentals of modern numerical techniques for a wide range of linear and nonlinear elliptic, parabolic, and hyperbolic partial differential and integral equations. Topics include mathematical formulations; finite difference, finite volume, finite element, and boundary element discretization methods; and direct and iterative solution techniques. The methodologies described form the foundation for computational approaches to engineering systems involving heat transfer, solid mechanics, fluid dynamics, and electromagnetics. Computer assignments requiring programming.
<br><I>Q. Wang, J. K. White</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.341"></a>
<p><h3>6.341 Discrete-Time Signal Processing
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.011">6.011</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/6.341/www/">http://web.mit.edu/6.341/www/</a>
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.341"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR11-12.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-124</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>F11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-145</a>) or <i>F2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-145</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Representation, analysis, and design of discrete time signals and systems. Decimation, interpolation, and sampling rate conversion. Noise shaping. Flowgraph structures for DT systems. Lattice filters. Time- and frequency-domain design techniques for IIR and FIR filters. Parametric signal modeling, linear prediction, and the relation to lattice filters. Discrete Fourier transform (DFT). Computation of the DFT including FFT algorithms. Short-time Fourier analysis and relation to filter banks.  Multirate techniques. Perfect reconstruction filter banks and their relation to wavelets.
<br><I>A. V. Oppenheim, J. Ward</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.344"></a>
<p><h3>6.344 Digital Image Processing
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)

<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Digital images as two-dimensional signals. Digital signal processing theories used for digital image processing, including one-dimensional and two-dimensional convolution, Fourier transform, discrete Fourier transform, and discrete cosine transform. Image processing basics. Image enhancement. Image restoration. Image coding and compression. Video processing including video coding and compression. Additional topics including digital high-definition television systems.
<br><I>J. S. Lim</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<p><h3>6.345[J] Automatic Speech Recognition
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)

<a name="6.374"></a>
<p><h3>6.374 Analysis and Design of Digital Integrated Circuits
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.012">6.012</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.004">6.004</a>
<br>Units: 3-3-6
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.374"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR11-12.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-302</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>TBA</i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Device and circuit level optimization of digital building blocks. MOS device models including Deep Sub-Micron effects. Circuit design styles for logic, arithmetic, and sequential blocks. Estimation and minimization of energy consumption. Interconnect models and parasitics, device sizing and logical effort, timing issues (clock skew and jitter), and active clock distribution techniques. Memory architectures, circuits (sense amplifiers), and devices. Testing of integrated circuits. Extensive custom and standard cell layout and simulation in design projects and software labs.
<br><I>V. Sze, A. P. Chandrakasan</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.375"></a>
<p><h3>6.375 Complex Digital Systems Design
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2018-2019" title="Not offered academic year 2018-2019" src="/icns/nonext.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.004">6.004</a>
<br>Units: 5-5-2
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to the design and implementation of large-scale digital systems using hardware description languages and high-level synthesis tools in conjunction with standard commercial electronic design automation (EDA) tools. Emphasizes modular and robust designs, reusable modules, correctness by construction, architectural exploration, meeting area and timing constraints, and developing functional field-programmable gate array (FPGA) prototypes. Extensive use of CAD tools in weekly labs serve as preparation for a multi-person design project on multi-million gate FPGAs. Enrollment may be limited.
<br><I>Arvind</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<h3>Probabilistic Systems and Communication</h3>
<a name="6.431A"></a>
<p><h3>6.431A Introduction to Probability I
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">); first half of term
<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6a.html#6.041A">6.041A</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=m2" title="18.02, 18.02A, 18.022, 18.023, 18.024">18.02</a>
<br>Units: 2-0-4
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.431A"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> Ends Oct 20. <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=2">2-190</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>TR11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=24">24-121</a>) or <i>TR12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=24">24-121</a>) or <i>TR1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=1">1-150</a>) or <i>TR2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=1">1-150</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Provides an introduction to probability theory and the modeling and analysis of probabilistic systems. Probabilistic models, conditional probability. Discrete and continuous random variables. Expectation and conditional expectation. Limit Theorems. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.
<br><I>P. Jaillet, J. N. Tsitsiklis</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.431B"></a>
<p><h3>6.431B Introduction to Probability II
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">); second half of term

<br>Prereq: <a href="m6b.html#6.431A">6.431A</a>
<br>Units: 2-0-4
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.431B"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> Begins Oct 23. <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=2">2-190</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>TR11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=24">24-121</a>) or <i>TR12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=24">24-121</a>) or <i>TR1</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=1">1-150</a>) or <i>TR2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=1">1-150</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Continuation of 6.431A. Further topics about random variables. Bayesian estimation and hypothesis testing. Elements of statistical inference. Bernoulli and Poisson processes. Markov chains. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.
<br><I>P. Jaillet, J. N. Tsitsiklis</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.434"></a>
<p><h3>6.434[J] Statistics for Engineers and Scientists
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m16a.html#16.391">16.391[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=m2" title="18.02, 18.02A, 18.022, 18.023, 18.024">18.02</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>, <a href="m6b.html#6.431B">6.431B</a>, or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.434"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW1-2.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=8">8-205</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Rigorous introduction to fundamentals of statistics motivated by engineering applications. Topics include exponential families, order statistics, sufficient statistics, estimation theory, hypothesis testing, measures of performance, notions of optimality, analysis of variance (ANOVA), simple linear regression, and selected topics.
<br><I>M. Win, J. N. Tsitsiklis</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.436"></a>
<p><h3>6.436[J] Fundamentals of Probability
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m15a.html#15.085">15.085[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=m2" title="18.02, 18.02A, 18.022, 18.023, 18.024">18.02</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.436"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW2.30-4</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=E51">E51-345</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>F2</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=66">66-144</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to probability theory. Probability spaces and measures. Discrete and continuous random variables. Conditioning and independence. Multivariate normal distribution. Abstract integration, expectation, and related convergence results. Moment generating and  characteristic functions. Bernoulli and Poisson process. Finite-state  Markov chains. Convergence notions and their relations. Limit theorems. Familiarity with elementary notions in probability and real analysis is desirable.
<br><I>J. N. Tsitsiklis, D. Gamarnik</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.437"></a>
<p><h3>6.437 Inference and Information
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.008">6.008</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.041B">6.041B</a>, or <a href="m6b.html#6.436">6.436</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to principles of Bayesian and non-Bayesian statistical inference. Hypothesis testing and parameter estimation, sufficient statistics; exponential families. EM agorithm. Log-loss inference criterion, entropy and model capacity.  Kullback-Leibler distance and information geometry. Asymptotic analysis and large deviations theory.  Model  order estimation; nonparametric statistics.  Computational issues and approximation techniques; Monte Carlo methods.  Selected special topics such as universal prediction and compression.
<br><I>P. Golland, G. W. Wornell</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.438"></a>
<p><h3>6.438 Algorithms for Inference
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.008">6.008</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.041B">6.041B</a>, or <a href="m6b.html#6.436">6.436</a>; <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.438"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR9.30-11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=4">4-370</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>F10</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=8">8-119</a>) or <i>F11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=8">8-119</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to statistical inference with probabilistic graphical models.  Directed and undirected graphical models, and factor graphs, over discrete and Gaussian distributions; hidden Markov models, linear dynamical systems.  Sum-product and junction tree algorithms; forward-backward algorithm, Kalman filtering and smoothing.  Min-sum and Viterbi algorithms.  Variational methods, mean-field theory, and loopy belief propagation.  Particle methods and filtering.  Building graphical models from data, including parameter estimation and structure learning; Baum-Welch and Chow-Liu algorithms.   Selected special topics.
<br><I>P. Golland, G. W. Wornell, D. Shah</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.440"></a>
<p><h3>6.440 Essential Coding Theory
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2018-2019" title="Not offered academic year 2018-2019" src="/icns/nonext.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.006">6.006</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.045">6.045</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces the theory of error-correcting codes. Focuses on the essential results in the area, taught from first principles. Special focus on results of asymptotic or algorithmic significance. Principal topics include construction and existence results for error-correcting codes; limitations on the combinatorial performance of error-correcting codes; decoding algorithms; and applications to other areas of mathematics and computer science.
<br><I>Staff</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.441"></a>
<p><h3>6.441 Information Theory
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.041B">6.041B</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/6.441/www/">http://web.mit.edu/6.441/www/</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Mathematical definitions of information measures, convexity, continuity, and variational properties. Lossless source coding; variable-length and block compression; Slepian-Wolf theorem; ergodic sources and Shannon-McMillan theorem. Hypothesis testing, large deviations and I-projection. Fundamental limits of block coding for noisy channels: capacity, dispersion, finite blocklength bounds. Coding with feedback. Joint source-channel problem. Rate-distortion theory, vector quantizers. Advanced topics include Gelfand-Pinsker problem, multiple access channels, broadcast channels  (depending on available time).
<br><I>M. Medard, Y. Polyanskiy, L. Zheng</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.442"></a>
<p><h3>6.442 Optical Networks
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2018-2019" title="Not offered academic year 2018-2019" src="/icns/nonext.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.041B">6.041B</a> or <a href="m6a.html#6.042">6.042</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduces the fundamental and practical aspects of optical network technology, architecture, design and analysis tools and techniques.  The treatment of optical networks are from the architecture and system design points of view. Optical hardware technologies are introduced and characterized as fundamental network building blocks on which optical transmission systems and network architectures are based. Beyond the Physical Layer, the higher network layers (Media Access Control, Network and Transport Layers) are treated together as integral parts of network design. Performance metrics, analysis and optimization techniques are developed to help guide the creation of high performance complex optical networks.
<br><I>V. W. S. Chan</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.443"></a>
<p><h3>6.443[J] Quantum Information Science
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m8b.html#8.371">8.371[J]</A>, <A HREF="m18a.html#18.436">18.436[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m18a.html#18.435">18.435</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Examines quantum computation and quantum information. Topics include quantum circuits, the quantum Fourier transform and search algorithms, the quantum operations formalism, quantum error correction, Calderbank-Shor-Steane and stabilizer codes, fault tolerant quantum computation, quantum data compression, quantum entanglement, capacity of quantum channels, and quantum cryptography and the proof of its security. Prior knowledge of quantum mechanics required.
<br><I>I. Chuang</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.450"></a>
<p><h3>6.450 Principles of Digital Communication
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.011">6.011</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Communication sources and channels; data compression; entropy and the AEP; Lempel-Ziv universal coding; scalar and vector quantization; L2 waveforms; signal space and its representation by sampling and other expansions; aliasing; the Nyquist criterion; PAM and QAM modulation; Gaussian noise and random processes; detection and optimal receivers; fading channels and wireless communication; introduction to communication system design.
<br><I>M. Medard, L. Zheng</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.452"></a>
<p><h3>6.452 Principles of Wireless Communication
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6b.html#6.450">6.450</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Introduction to design, analysis, and fundamental limits of wireless transmission systems.  Wireless channel and system models; fading and diversity; resource management and power control; multiple-antenna and MIMO systems; space-time codes and decoding algorithms; multiple-access techniques and multiuser detection; broadcast codes and precoding; cellular and ad-hoc network topologies; OFDM and ultrawideband systems; architectural issues.
<br><I>G. W. Wornell, L. Zheng</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.453"></a>
<p><h3>6.453 Quantum Optical Communication
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.011">6.011</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Quantum optics: Dirac notation quantum mechanics; harmonic oscillator quantization; number states, coherent states, and squeezed states; radiation field quantization and quantum field propagation; P-representation and classical fields. Linear loss and linear amplification: commutator preservation and the Uncertainty Principle; beam splitters; phase-insensitive and phase-sensitive amplifiers. Quantum photodetection: direct detection, heterodyne detection, and homodyne detection. Second-order nonlinear optics: phasematched interactions; optical parametric amplifiers; generation of squeezed states, photon-twin beams, non-classical fourth-order interference, and polarization entanglement. Quantum systems theory: optimum binary detection; quantum precision measurements; quantum cryptography; and quantum teleportation.
<br><I>J. H. Shapiro</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.454"></a>
<p><h3>6.454 Graduate Seminar in Area I
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">) <img src="/icns/repeat.gif" alt="Can be repeated for credit" title="Can be repeated for credit" width=16 height=16 align="bottom">
<br>Prereq: Permission of instructor
<br>Units: 2-0-4
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/6.454/www/">http://web.mit.edu/6.454/www/</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Student-run advanced graduate seminar with focus on topics in  communications, control, signal processing, optimization. Participants give presentations outside of their own research to expose colleagues to topics not covered in the usual curriculum. Recent topics have included compressed sensing, MDL principle, communication complexity, linear programming decoding, biology in EECS, distributed hypothesis testing, algorithms for random satisfaction problems, and cryptogaphy.  Open to advanced students from all areas of EECS. Limited to 12.
<br><I>L. Zheng, D. Shah</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.456"></a>
<p><h3>6.456 Array Processing
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6b.html#6.341">6.341</a>; <a href="m2b.html#2.687">2.687</a>, or <a href="m6a.html#6.011">6.011</a> and <a href="m18a.html#18.06">18.06</a>
<br>Units: 3-2-7
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Adaptive and non-adaptive processing of signals received at arrays of sensors. Deterministic beamforming, space-time random processes, optimal and adaptive algorithms, and the sensitivity of algorithm performance to modeling errors and limited data. Methods of improving the robustness of algorithms to modeling errors and limited data are derived.  Advanced topics include an introduction to matched field processing and physics-based methods of estimating signal statistics. Homework exercises providing the opportunity to implement and analyze the performance of algorithms in processing data supplied during the course.
<br><I>Staff</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<h3>Bioelectrical Engineering</h3>
<a name="6.503"></a>
<p><h3>6.503 Foundations of Algorithms and Computational Techniques in Systems Biology
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6b.html#6.581">6.581[J]</A>, <A HREF="m20a.html#20.482">20.482[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.021">6.021</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.034">6.034</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.046">6.046</a>, <a href="m6b.html#6.336">6.336</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.417">18.417</a>, or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Illustrates computational approaches to solving problems in systems biology. Uses a series of case studies to demonstrate how an effective match between the statement of a biological problem and the selection of an appropriate algorithm or computational technique can lead to fundamental advances. Covers several discrete and numerical algorithms used in simulation, feature extraction, and optimization for molecular, network, and systems models in biology. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.
<br><I>B. Tidor</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.521"></a>
<p><h3>6.521[J] Cellular Neurophysiology and Computing
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2b.html#2.794">2.794[J]</A>, <A HREF="m9a.html#9.021">9.021[J]</A>, <A HREF="m20a.html#20.470">20.470[J]</A>, <A HREF="mHSTa.html#HST.541">HST.541[J]</A>)<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m2b.html#2.791">2.791[J]</A>, <A HREF="m6a.html#6.021">6.021[J]</A>, <A HREF="m9a.html#9.21">9.21[J]</A>, <A HREF="m20a.html#20.370">20.370[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p2" title="8.02, 8.021, 8.022">8.02</a>; <a href="m18a.html#18.03">18.03</a>; <a href="m2a.html#2.005">2.005</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.002">6.002</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.003">6.003</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.071">6.071</a>, <a href="m10a.html#10.301">10.301</a>, <a href="m20a.html#20.110">20.110</a>, or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 5-2-5
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.521"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW11-12.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-124</a>) <b>Lab:</b> <i>TBA</i> <b>Recitation:</b> <i>T12</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-303</a>) or <i>T4</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=34">34-302</a>) <i><b>+final</b></i><!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Integrated overview of the biophysics of cells from prokaryotes to neurons, with a focus on mass transport and electrical signal generation across cell membrane. First third of course focuses on mass transport through membranes: diffusion, osmosis, chemically mediated, and active transport. Second third focuses on electrical properties of cells: ion transport to action potential generation and propagation in electrically excitable cells. Synaptic transmission. Electrical properties interpreted via kinetic and molecular properties of single voltage-gated ion channels. Final third focuses on biophysics of synaptic transmission and introduction to neural computing. Laboratory and computer exercises illustrate the concepts. Students taking graduate version complete different assignments.
<br><I>J. Han, T. Heldt</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.522"></a>
<p><h3>6.522[J] Quantitative Physiology: Organ Transport Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)

<br>Prereq: <a href="m2a.html#2.006">2.006</a> or <a href="m6a.html#6.013">6.013</a>; <a href="m6a.html#6.021">6.021</a>
<br>Units: 4-2-6
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Application of the principles of energy and mass flow to major human organ systems. Mechanisms of regulation and homeostasis. Anatomical, physiological and pathophysiological features of the cardiovascular, respiratory and renal systems. Systems, features and devices that are most illuminated by the methods of physical sciences. Laboratory work includes some animal studies. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.<br>Application of the principles of energy and mass flow to major human organ systems. Mechanisms of regulation and homeostasis. Anatomical, physiological and pathophysiological features of the cardiovascular, respiratory and renal systems. Systems, features and devices that are most illuminated by the methods of physical sciences. Laboratory work includes some animal studies. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.
<br><I>T. Heldt, R. G. Mark, C. M. Stultz</I><br>

<p><h3>6.524[J] Molecular, Cellular, and Tissue Biomechanics
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2b.html#2.798">2.798[J]</A>, <A HREF="m3b.html#3.971">3.971[J]</A>, <A HREF="m10a.html#10.537">10.537[J]</A>, <A HREF="m20a.html#20.410">20.410[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=b" title="7.012, 7.013, 7.014, 7.015, 7.016">7.012</a>; <a href="m2a.html#2.002">2.002</a>, <a href="m2a.html#2.006">2.006</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.013">6.013</a>, <a href="m10a.html#10.301">10.301</a>, or <a href="m10a.html#10.302">10.302</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.524"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> TBA. <!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Develops and applies scaling laws and the methods of continuum mechanics to biomechanical phenomena over a range of length scales. Topics include structure of tissues and the molecular basis for macroscopic properties; chemical and electrical effects on mechanical behavior; cell mechanics, motility and adhesion; biomembranes; biomolecular mechanics and molecular motors. Experimental methods for probing structures at the tissue, cellular, and molecular levels.
<br><I>R. D. Kamm, K. J. Van Vliet</I><br>No textbook information available

<p><h3>6.525[J] Medical Device Design
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2b.html#2.75">2.75[J]</A>, <A HREF="mHSTa.html#HST.552">HST.552[J]</A>)<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m2b.html#2.750">2.750[J]</A>, <A HREF="m6a.html#6.025">6.025[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m2a.html#2.008">2.008</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.101">6.101</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.111">6.111</a>, <a href="m6a.html#6.115">6.115</a>, <a href="m22a.html#22.071">22.071</a>, or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.525"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW1-2.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=3">3-270</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Application of mechanical and electrical engineering fundamentals to the design of medical devices that address clinical needs. Students work in small teams on a major project to translate a clinical challenge into a proof-of-concept prototype device. Students conduct user analysis, develop design specifications, and follow a structured process to cultivate creative designs and apply analytical techniques to optimize them. They deepen their understanding of art and intellectual property by researching prior representations. Develops practical skills in prototyping and testing as well as project management. Includes lectures, problem sets and exams that focus on design fundamentals. Instruction and practice in written and oral communication provided. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments. Enrollment limited.
<br><I>A. H. Slocum, G. Hom</I><br>No textbook information available

<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>

<br>Units: 2-2-8
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Experimental investigations of speech processes. Topics: measurement of articulatory movements; measurements of pressures and airflows in speech production; computer-aided waveform analysis and spectral analysis of speech; synthesis of speech; perception and discrimination of speechlike sounds; speech prosody; models for speech recognition; speech development; and other topics. Recommended prerequisites: 6.002 or 18.03.
<br><I>L. D. Braida, S. Shattuck-Hufnagel</I><br>

<p><h3>6.555[J] Biomedical Signal and Image Processing
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m16a.html#16.456">16.456[J]</A>, <A HREF="mHSTa.html#HST.582">HST.582[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.003">6.003</a>, <a href="m2a.html#2.004">2.004</a>, <a href="m16a.html#16.002">16.002</a>, or <a href="m18a.html#18.085">18.085</a>
<br>Units: 3-3-6
<br>URL: <a href="http://web.mit.edu/6.555/www/">http://web.mit.edu/6.555/www/</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Fundamentals of digital signal processing with emphasis on problems in biomedical research and clinical medicine. Basic principles and algorithms for processing both deterministic and random signals. Topics include data acquisition, imaging, filtering, coding, feature extraction, and modeling. Lab projects, performed in MATLAB, provide practical experience in processing physiological data, with examples from cardiology, speech processing, and medical imaging. Lectures cover signal processing topics relevant to the lab exercises, as well as background on the biological signals processed in the labs.
<br><I>J. Greenberg, E. Adalsteinsson, W. Wells</I><br>

<p><h3>6.556[J] Data Acquisition and Image Reconstruction in MRI
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="mHSTa.html#HST.580">HST.580[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.011">6.011</a>
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.556"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR11-12.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=1">1-150</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Applies analysis of signals and noise in linear systems, sampling, and Fourier properties to magnetic resonance (MR) imaging acquisition and reconstruction. Provides adequate foundation for MR physics to enable study of RF excitation design, efficient Fourier sampling, parallel encoding, reconstruction of non-uniformly sampled data, and the impact of hardware imperfections on reconstruction performance. Surveys active areas of MR research. Assignments include Matlab-based work with real data. Includes visit to a scan site for human MR studies.
<br><I>E. Adalsteinsson</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->

<p><h3>6.557[J] Biomolecular Feedback Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2a.html#2.18">2.18[J]</A>)<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m2a.html#2.180">2.180[J]</A>, <A HREF="m6a.html#6.027">6.027[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m18a.html#18.03">18.03</a>, <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=b" title="7.012, 7.013, 7.014, 7.015, 7.016">7.012</a>, or permission of instructor

Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.
<br><I>D. Del Vecchio, R. Weiss</I><br>

<a name="6.561"></a>
<p><h3>6.561[J] Fields, Forces, and Flows in Biological Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m2b.html#2.795">2.795[J]</A>, <A HREF="m10a.html#10.539">10.539[J]</A>, <A HREF="m20a.html#20.430">20.430[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: Permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.561"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>MW1-2.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-124</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Molecular diffusion, diffusion-reaction, conduction, convection in biological systems; fields in heterogeneous media; electrical double layers; Maxwell stress tensor, electrical forces in physiological systems. Fluid and solid continua: equations of motion useful for porous, hydrated biological tissues. Case studies of membrane transport, electrode interfaces, electrical, mechanical, and chemical transduction in tissues, convective-diffusion/reaction, electrophoretic, electroosmotic flows in tissues/MEMs, and ECG. Electromechanical and physicochemical interactions in cells and biomaterials; musculoskeletal, cardiovascular, and other biological and clinical examples. Prior undergraduate coursework in transport recommended.
<br><I>M. Bathe, A. J. Grodzinsky</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->

<p><h3>6.581[J] Foundations of Algorithms and Computational Techniques in Systems Biology

<p><h3>6.602 Fundamentals of Photonics
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)

<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">

Topics include classical ray, wave, beam, and Fourier optics; Maxwell's electromagnetic waves; resonators; quantum theory of photons; light-matter interaction; laser amplification; lasers; and semiconductors optoelectronics. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.

<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
