<a name="6.901"></a>
<p><h3>6.901[J] Innovation Engineering: Moving Ideas to Impact
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m15b.html#15.359">15.359[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 3-3-6
<br>URL: <a href="http://www.mit.edu:8001/courses/6.901/patent.html">http://www.mit.edu:8001/courses/6.901/patent.html</a>
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.901"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR9-10.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=1">1-390</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Designed for students to gain the perspective of a Chief Technology Officer of a start-up, large corporation, or a not-for-profit. Details the innovation process, from an idea's inception through impact in the economy, regardless of organizational setting. Explores how solutions are developed to become ready for broader market deployment. Includes testing and development of the problem-solution fit, probing of solutions for robustness, and testing of both technical and operational scaling of proposed solutions. Examines the human aspects of innovation, specifically issues of team building and readiness. Considers the broader system for innovation, including the role of key stakeholders in shaping its success in order to arrive at an impactful solution. Addresses intellectual property, the effect of regulations and social and cultural differences across varied global markets, and the personal skillset necessary to align and manage these issues.
<br><I>V. Bulovic, F. Murray</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.902"></a>
<p><h3>6.902 Engineering Innovation and Design
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Engineering School-Wide Elective Subject. <br>(Offered under: <A HREF="m2b.html#2.723">2.723</A>, <A HREF="m6c.html#6.902">6.902</A>, <A HREF="m16b.html#16.662">16.662</A>)
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 2-1-3
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.902"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>M EVE (7-9 PM)</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=35">35-225</a>) <b>Recitation:</b> <i>M EVE (9 PM)</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=35">35-225</a>) or <i>W EVE (7 PM)</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=2">2-105</a>) or <i>W EVE (8 PM)</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=2">2-105</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Project-based seminar in innovative design thinking develops students' ability to conceive, implement, and evaluate successful projects in any engineering discipline. Lectures focus on the iterative design process and techniques to enhance creative analysis. Students use this process to design and implement robust voice recognition applications using a simple web-based system. They also give presentations and receive feedback to sharpen their communication skills for high emotional and intellectual impact. Guest lectures illustrate multidisciplinary approaches to design thinking.
<br><I>B. Kotelly</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.903"></a>
<p><h3>6.903 Patents, Copyrights, and the Law of Intellectual Property
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 2-0-4
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Intensive introduction to the US law of intellectual property with major emphasis on patents, including the process of patent application and the remedies for patent infringement.  Also focuses on copyrights and provides a brief look at trademarks and trade secrets. Presents comparisons of what can and cannot be protected, and what rights the owner does and does not obtain. Highlights issues relating to information technology, biogenetic materials, and business methods. Readings include judicial opinions and statutory material. No listeners.
<br><I>S. M. Bauer</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.904"></a>
<p><h3>6.904 Ethics for Engineers
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Engineering School-Wide Elective Subject. <br>(Offered under: <A HREF="m1a.html#1.082">1.082</A>, <A HREF="m2c.html#2.900">2.900</A>, <A HREF="m6c.html#6.904">6.904</A>, <A HREF="m10a.html#10.01">10.01</A>, <A HREF="m22a.html#22.014">22.014</A>)<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6c.html#6.9041">6.9041</A>)
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 2-0-4
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.904"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>M3-5</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=66">66-144</a>) or <i>T3-5</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=37">37-212</a>) or <i>T EVE (7.30-9.30 PM)</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=66">66-144</a>) or <i>W3-5</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=36">36-153</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Integrates classical readings that provide an overview of ethics with a survey of case studies that focus on ethical problems arising in the practice of engineering. Readings taken from a variety of sources, such as Aristotle, Machiavelli, Bacon, Hobbes, Locke, the Founding Fathers, and the Bible. Case studies include written analyses and films that address engineering disasters, biotechnology, court cases, ethical codes, and the ultimate scope and aims of engineering. Students taking independent inquiry version 6.9041 expand the scope of their term project.
<br><I>D. Doneson, B. L. Trout</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->

<p><h3>6.9041 Ethics for Engineers - Independent Inquiry
<br>(New)
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>

<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m1a.html#1.082">1.082[J]</A>, <A HREF="m2c.html#2.900">2.900[J]</A>, <A HREF="m6c.html#6.904">6.904[J]</A>, <A HREF="m10a.html#10.01">10.01[J]</A>, <A HREF="m22a.html#22.014">22.014[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 2-0-10
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.9041"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>M3-5</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=66">66-144</a>) or <i>T3-5</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=37">37-212</a>) or <i>T EVE (7.30-9.30 PM)</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=66">66-144</a>) or <i>W3-5</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=36">36-153</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">

Readings taken from a variety of sources, such as Aristotle, Machiavelli, Bacon, Hobbes, Locke, the Founding Fathers, and the Bible. Case studies include written analyses and films that address engineering disasters, biotechnology, court cases, ethical codes, and the ultimate scope and aims of engineering. To satisfy the independent inquiry component of this subject, students expand the scope of their term project.

<a name="6.905"></a>
<p><h3>6.905 Large-scale Symbolic Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6c.html#6.945">6.945</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.034">6.034</a> or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Concepts and techniques for the design and implementation of large software systems that can be adapted to uses not anticipated by the designer. Applications include compilers, computer-algebra systems, deductive systems, and some artificial intelligence applications. Covers means for decoupling goals from strategy, mechanisms for implementing additive data-directed invocation, work with partially-specified entities, and how to manage multiple viewpoints. Topics include combinators, generic operations, pattern matching, pattern-directed invocation, rule systems, backtracking, dependencies, indeterminacy, memoization, constraint propagation, and incremental refinement. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.
<br><I>G. J. Sussman</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.906"></a>
<p><h3>6.906 StartMIT: Workshop for Entrepreneurs and Innovators
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="IAP" title="IAP" src="/icns/iap.gif">)

<br>Units: 4-0-2 [P/D/F]

<br>Designed for students who are interested in entrepreneurship and want to explore the potential commercialization of their research project. Introduces practices for building a successful company, such as idea creation and validation, defining a value proposition, building a team, marketing, customer traction, and possible funding models. Students taking graduate version complete different assignments.
<br><I>A. Chandrakasan</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<p><h3>6.911 Engineering Leadership Lab
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/repeat.gif" alt="Can be repeated for credit" title="Can be repeated for credit" width=16 height=16 align="bottom">
<br>Engineering School-Wide Elective Subject. <br>(Offered under: <A HREF="m6c.html#6.911">6.911</A>, <A HREF="m16b.html#16.650">16.650</A>)<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6c.html#6.913">6.913[J]</A>, <A HREF="m16b.html#16.667">16.667[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: None. <I><a href="m6c.html#6.912">6.912</a></I> or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 0-2-1
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.911"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lab:</b> <i>F9-11</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-124</a>) or <i>F1-3</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-124</a>) or <i>F3-5</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-124</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Exposes students to leadership frameworks, models and cases within an engineering context, in an interactive, practice-based environment, honing leadership and teamwork skills. Students participate in guided reflections on individual and team successes, and discover opportunities for improvement in controlled settings. Activities include design-implement activities, role-plays, simulations, small group discussions, and performance and peer assessments by and of other students. Content throughout the term is frequently student-driven. First year Gordon Engineering Leadership Program (GEL) students register for 6.911. Second year GEL Program students register for 6.913. Preference to students enrolled in the Bernard M. Gordon-MIT Engineering Leadership Program.
<br><I>L. McGonagle, J. Feiler</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->

<p><h3>6.912 Engineering Leadership
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">) <img src="/icns/repeat.gif" alt="Can be repeated for credit" title="Can be repeated for credit" width=16 height=16 align="bottom">
<br>Engineering School-Wide Elective Subject. <br>(Offered under: <A HREF="m6c.html#6.912">6.912</A>, <A HREF="m16b.html#16.651">16.651</A>)

<br>Units: 1-0-2
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.912"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>M9-10.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=5">5-233</a>) or <i>M11-12.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=5">5-233</a>) or <i>T9-10.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=5">5-233</a>) or <i>T11-12.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=5">5-233</a>)<!--s-->

May be repeated for credit once with permission of instructor. Preference to first-year students in the Gordon Engineering Leadership Program.

<a name="6.914"></a>
<p><h3>6.914 Project Engineering
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="IAP" title="IAP" src="/icns/iap.gif">)
<br>Engineering School-Wide Elective Subject. <br>(Offered under: <A HREF="m6c.html#6.914">6.914</A>, <A HREF="m16b.html#16.669">16.669</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6c.html#6.911">6.911</a> or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 1-2-1 [P/D/F]
<br>Credit cannot also be received for <A HREF="m1a.html#1.040">1.040</A>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Students attend a four-day off-site workshop where an introduction to basic principles, methods, and tools for project management in a realistic context are covered. In teams, students create a plan for a project of their choice in one of several areas, including aircraft modification, factory automation, enterprise software, flood prevention engineering, solar farm engineering, among others. Develops skills applicable to the management of complex development projects. Topics include cost-benefit analysis, resource and cost estimation, and project control and delivery, which are practiced during an experimental, team-based activity. Case studies highlight projects in both hardware/construction and software. Preference to students in the Bernard M. Gordon-MIT Engineering Leadership Program.
<br><I>O. de Weck, J. Feiler, L. McGonagle</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.915"></a>
<p><h3>6.915[J] Leading Innovation in Teams
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m16b.html#16.671">16.671[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 3-0-6
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Empowers future innovators in engineering and technology with a foundation of leadership and teamwork skills. Grounded in research but practical in focus, equips students with leadership competencies such as building self-awareness, motivating and developing others, influencing without authority, managing conflict, and communicating effectively.  Teamwork skills include how to convene, launch, and develop various types of teams, including project teams. Reviews recent advances in implementing innovations and building personal capacity for lifelong learning as a leading innovator. Enrollment limited to seating capacity of classroom. Admittance may be controlled by lottery.
<br><I>D. Nino, J. Schindall</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>

<p><h3>6.928[J] Leading Creative Teams
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m16b.html#16.990">16.990[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 3-1-5
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.928"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>F9.30-12.30</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=5">5-233</a>)<!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Prepares students to lead teams charged with developing creative solutions to challenging problems. Grounded in research but practical in focus, covers the development of basic leadership capabilities, such as motivating and influencing others, delegating, managing conflict, and communicating effectively; how to create, launch, develop, and adjourn teams; and how to foster creativity in small groups.

<br>Units: 4-0-8
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.933"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> <b>Lecture:</b> <i>TR EVE (7-9 PM)</i> (<a href="http://whereis.mit.edu/map-jpg?mapterms=32">32-141</a>)<!--s-->

Suitable for students interested in transforming an idea into a business or other realization for wide-scale societal impact. <a name="6.935"></a>
<p><h3>6.935[J] Financial Market Dynamics and Human Behavior
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m15b.html#15.481">15.481[J]</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m15b.html#15.401">15.401</a>, <a href="m15b.html#15.414">15.414</a>, or <a href="m15b.html#15.415">15.415</a>
<br>Units: 4-0-5
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Develops a new perspective on the dynamics of financial markets and the roles that human behavior and the business environment play in determining the evolution of behavior and institutions. Draws on a variety of disciplines to develop a more complete understanding of human behavior in the specific context of markets and other economic institutions. Incorporates practical applications from financial markets, the hedge fund industry, private equity, government regulation, and political economy. Students use ideas from this new perspective to formulate several new hypotheses regarding recent challenges to traditional economic thinking.
<br><I>A. Lo</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<a name="6.941"></a>
<p><h3>6.941 Statistics for Research Projects: Statistical Modeling and Experiment Design
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="IAP" title="IAP" src="/icns/iap.gif">)<br>Not offered regularly; consult department
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 2-2-2 [P/D/F]
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Practical introduction to data analysis, statistical modeling, and experimental design, intended to provide essential skills for conducting research.   Covers basic techniques such as hypothesis-testing and regression models for both traditional experiments and newer paradignms such as evaluating simulations.  Assignments reinforce techniques through analyzing sample datasets and reading case studies. Students with research projects will be encouraged to share their experiences and project-specific questions.
<br><I>Staff</I><br>

<a name="6.945"></a>
<p><h3>6.945 Large-scale Symbolic Systems
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m6c.html#6.905">6.905</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m6a.html#6.034">6.034</a> or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-0-9
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Concepts and techniques for the design and implementation of large software systems that can be adapted to uses not anticipated by the designer. Applications include compilers, computer-algebra systems, deductive systems, and some artificial intelligence applications. Covers means for decoupling goals from strategy, mechanisms for implementing additive data-directed invocation, work with partially-specified entities, and how to manage multiple viewpoints. Topics include combinators, generic operations, pattern matching, pattern-directed invocation, rule systems, backtracking, dependencies, indeterminacy, memoization, constraint propagation, and incremental refinement. Students taking graduate version complete additional assignments.
<br><I>G. J. Sussman</I><br>
</p><!--end-->
<a name="6.946"></a>
<p><h3>6.946[J] Classical Mechanics: A Computational Approach
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" title="Not offered academic year 2017-2018" src="/icns/nooffer.gif"><img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Graduate" title="Graduate" src="/icns/grad.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">)
<br>(Same subject as <A HREF="m8b.html#8.351">8.351[J]</A>, <A HREF="m12c.html#12.620">12.620[J]</A>)<br>(Subject meets with <A HREF="m12a.html#12.008">12.008</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="./search.cgi?search=&cred=p1" title="8.01, 8.01L, 8.011, 8.012">8.01</a>, <a href="m18a.html#18.03">18.03</a>, permission of instructor
<br>Units: 3-3-6
<br>URL: <a href="http://swissnet.ai.mit.edu/~gjs/6946/index.html">http://swissnet.ai.mit.edu/~gjs/6946/index.html</a>
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Classical mechanics in a computational framework, Lagrangian formulation, action, variational principles, and Hamilton's principle. Conserved quantities, Hamiltonian formulation, surfaces of section, chaos, and Liouville's theorem. Poincar&eacute; integral invariants, Poincar&eacute;-Birkhoff and KAM theorems. Invariant curves and cantori. Nonlinear resonances, resonance overlap and transition to chaos. Symplectic integration. Adiabatic invariants. Applications to simple physical systems and solar system dynamics. Extensive use of computation to capture methods, for simulation, and for symbolic analysis. Programming experience required. Students taking the graduate version complete additional assignments.
<br><I>J. Wisdom, G. J. Sussman</I><br>
</p><!--end-->

<a name="6.EPE"></a>
<p><h3>6.EPE UPOP Engineering Practice Experience
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Spring" title="Spring" src="/icns/spring.gif">)
<br>Engineering School-Wide Elective Subject. <br>(Offered under: <A HREF="m1c.html#1.EPE">1.EPE</A>, <A HREF="m2c.html#2.EPE">2.EPE</A>, <A HREF="m3b.html#3.EPE">3.EPE</A>, <A HREF="m6c.html#6.EPE">6.EPE</A>, <A HREF="m10b.html#10.EPE">10.EPE</A>, <A HREF="m16a.html#16.EPE">16.EPE</A>, <A HREF="m22a.html#22.EPE">22.EPE</A>)
<br>Prereq: <a href="m2c.html#2.EPW">2.EPW</a> or permission of instructor
<br>Units: 0-0-1 [P/D/F]
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.EPE"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> TBA. <!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Provides sophomores with guided practice in finding opportunities and excelling in the world of practice. Building on the skills and relationships acquired in the Engineering Practice Workshop, students receive coaching to articulate goals, invoke the UPOP network of mentors and employers, identify and pursue opportunities and negotiate terms of their summer assignment. Students complete a 10-12 week internship, which includes filing three progress reports, conducting one informational interview, and possibly hosting a site visit by MIT staff.  Returning to campus as juniors, UPOP students take part in reflective exercises that aid assimilation of learning objectives and reinforce the cognitive link between all aspects of the UPOP experience and disciplinary fields of study. Sequence begins in the spring of sophomore year and ends in the fall of junior year.
<br><I>Staff</I><br>No textbook information available
<a name="6.EPW"></a>
<p><h3>6.EPW UPOP Engineering Practice Workshop
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif"></h3>
<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Undergrad" title="Undergrad" src="/icns/under.gif">  (<img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="Fall" title="Fall" src="/icns/fall.gif">, <img width=16 height=16 align="bottom" alt="IAP" title="IAP" src="/icns/iap.gif">)
<br>Engineering School-Wide Elective Subject. <br>(Offered under: <A HREF="m1c.html#1.EPW">1.EPW</A>, <A HREF="m2c.html#2.EPW">2.EPW</A>, <A HREF="m3b.html#3.EPW">3.EPW</A>, <A HREF="m6c.html#6.EPW">6.EPW</A>, <A HREF="m10b.html#10.EPW">10.EPW</A>, <A HREF="m16a.html#16.EPW">16.EPW</A>, <A HREF="m20a.html#20.EPW">20.EPW</A>, <A HREF="m22a.html#22.EPW">22.EPW</A>)
<br>Prereq: None
<br>Units: 1-0-0 [P/D/F]
<br><a href="editcookie.cgi?add=6.EPW"><img align="bottom" border=1 width=16 height=16 alt="Add to schedule" title="Add to schedule" src="/icns/button0.gif"></a> TBA. <!--s-->
<br><img alt="______" src="/icns/hr.gif">
<br>Develops foundational skills for the world of practice in science, technology, and engineering. Sophomores receive classroom instruction, and one-on-one and small-group coaching in basics of professional identity building. They attend field trips to local employers and receive job interview practice, coached by industry volunteers. Over IAP, students attend a weeklong Team Training Camp of experiential learning modules - led by MIT faculty with the help of MIT alums and other senior professionals in business, engineering, and science where students participate in creative simulations, team problem-solving challenges, and oral presentations, and practice networking with employers. Enrollment limited.
<br><I>Staff</I><br>No textbook information available
</p><!--end-->
